**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

**Area 2: Economic Policy**

**Topic 2.1: International Trade and Tariffs**

The administration is dramatically escalating its international trade conflict on multiple fronts. President Trump has announced new 30% tariffs against both the European Union and Mexico, with a declared effective date of August 1st [1]. This action marks a significant intensification of the trade war with two of the largest U.S. trading partners. In a separate, highly targeted action, the U.S. has imposed 50% tariffs on Brazil. A Reuters analysis asserts this specific measure is not aimed at correcting a trade imbalance but is instead designed to "directly coerce its judiciary" [2], signaling a novel use of trade policy as a tool for geopolitical leverage.

**Topic 2.2: Domestic Economy, Inflation, and the Federal Reserve**

Tensions between the White House and the Federal Reserve are increasing, fueling high-level speculation about the stability of the central bank's independent leadership. A "huge deal" White House probe into the Federal Reserve is reportedly underway, prompting speculation that President Trump may seek to oust Chair Jerome Powell [1]. This maneuver is part of a broader pattern of White House attacks that have already forced the Fed to publicly defend its spending on renovations [2]. These political pressures are mounting as economic forecasts predict a tangible rise in U.S. inflation, which is being directly linked to the expected pass-through effects of the administration's newly announced tariffs [3].

**Area 3: Immigration and Border Security**

**Topic 3.1: DHS/ICE Enforcement, Detention, and Legal Challenges**

The administration’s immigration enforcement tactics are facing major legal defeats and generating significant controversy. Controversial tactics continue to draw public condemnation, including a widely reported incident where ICE agents handcuffed a 71-year-old U.S. citizen grandmother at a San Diego immigration court [3]. Meanwhile, Democratic lawmakers are planning a high-profile visit to a detention center nicknamed "Alligator Alcatraz," which has been described in media reports as a site of "surreal brand of stylized cruelty" [4].

**Area 4: Domestic Policy and Public Discourse**

**Topic 4.1: Texas Floods: Federal Disaster Response and FEMA Scrutiny**

The federal response to the deadly floods in Texas is under severe scrutiny, focusing on both pre-disaster regulatory decisions by FEMA and critical operational failures during the crisis. Reports reveal that years before the flood, FEMA removed dozens of buildings at a Texas youth camp, "Camp Mystic," from the 100-year flood map. This de-regulation enabled the camp's expansion into what was a known flood hazard zone, where the disaster later struck [1]. During the emergency response, DHS Secretary Kristi Noem fired FEMA contractors, after which the agency reportedly missed thousands of calls from desperate flood victims, an action one report called "'unforgivable'" [2]. President Trump visited Texas to defend the response, which some local officials praised, but he also "lashed out" at critical questions from the media [3]. The disaster has revived public focus on the President's past statements about wanting to eliminate FEMA entirely [4].

## 3. Immigration and Border Security

### 3.1. DHS/ICE Enforcement, Detention, and Legal Challenges

The administration’s immigration enforcement tactics are facing major legal defeats and generating significant controversy. An L.A. judge has ordered a halt to a "chaotic and relentless 36-day immigration crackdown" in Southern California, specifically ordering agents to cease "roving patrols" and what the court described as "indiscriminately rounding up" immigrants based on racial profiling [1]. The administration has already announced its intent to appeal this restrictive order [2]. Controversial tactics continue to draw public condemnation, including a widely reported incident where ICE agents handcuffed a 71-year-old U.S. citizen grandmother at a San Diego immigration court [3]. Meanwhile, Democratic lawmakers are planning a high-profile visit to a detention center nicknamed "Alligator Alcatraz," which has been described in media reports as a site of "surreal brand of stylized cruelty" [4].

### 3.2. Immigration Policy and Legislative Reform

The administration is actively pursuing a major expansion of its immigration detention and enforcement infrastructure. Reports indicate ICE is "set to vastly expand its reach with new funds" [1], a move complemented by Homeland Security Secretary Kristi Noem's confirmation that she is in talks with five Republican-led states to construct a new detention site [2]. On the legislative front, a proposal known as the "Big Beautiful Bill" is advancing, which is expected to enact major changes to both criminal justice and immigration law [3]. In an apparent concession to industry pressure, President Trump has reportedly offered a new visa program for migrant workers following significant backlash from the agricultural sector [4]. In Congress, a counter-measure has been introduced by Senator Elissa Slotkin, whose legislation would increase transparency by requiring immigration officers to display clear identification [5].

The administration's deportation policies are encountering direct resistance from foreign governments. A Nigerian minister has publicly stated the country "can't take deportees from US," asserting that Nigeria has "enough problems" of its own to manage [1]. Separately, a case that highlights the complexities and potential consequences of U.S. immigration policy involves a pro-Trump father, a green card holder who has resided in the U.S. since age three, who is now reportedly stuck in Canada after being denied re-entry into the United States [2].

## 4. Domestic Policy and Public Discourse

### 4.1. Texas Floods: Federal Disaster Response and FEMA Scrutiny

The federal response to the deadly floods in Texas is under severe scrutiny, focusing on both pre-disaster regulatory decisions by FEMA and critical operational failures during the crisis. Reports reveal that years before the flood, FEMA removed dozens of buildings at a Texas youth camp, "Camp Mystic," from the 100-year flood map. This de-regulation enabled the camp's expansion into what was a known flood hazard zone, where the disaster later struck [1]. During the emergency response, DHS Secretary Kristi Noem fired FEMA contractors, after which the agency reportedly missed thousands of calls from desperate flood victims, an action one report called "'unforgivable'" [2]. President Trump visited Texas to defend the response, which some local officials praised, but he also "lashed out" at critical questions from the media [3]. The disaster has revived public focus on the President's past statements about wanting to eliminate FEMA entirely [4].

**References:**
[1] Dozens of Camp Mystic buildings removed from 100-year flood map by FEMA before expansion, records show, https://www.cbsnews.com/news/texas-flood-camp-mystic-buildings-removed-from-100-year-flood-map-by-fema/  
[2] 'Unforgivable': FEMA Missed Thousands of Calls from Texas Flood Victims After Noem Fired Contractors, https://www.commondreams.org/news/fema-missed-calls-texas-floods  
[3] Trump defends federal government’s response to Hill Country floods during Texas visit | The president met with state and local officials, who praised the White House response, and lashed out at a question on whether aid and rescue efforts occurred fast enough., https://www.texastribune.org/2025/07/11/trump-texas-visit-kerrville-floods-fema-defends-criticism/

### 4.2. Health, Science, and Social Policy

The administration is advancing several contentious policies in the domains of health and science. U.S. officials are reportedly "targeting mRNA vaccines," a development that is creating what sources describe as "tremendous uncertainty" for critical cancer research [1]. Furthermore, reports indicate an internal plan within the administration to leverage artificial intelligence for the purpose of denying Medicare authorizations [2]. In a separate matter, Attorney General Pam Bondi has announced the dismissal of federal charges against a plastic surgeon who was accused of creating and distributing fake COVID-19 vaccine cards [3]. This policy environment exists as threats against local school officials have reportedly nearly tripled since the outset of the COVID-19 pandemic [4].

The U.S. posture on European security is undergoing a significant and closely watched shift. Secretary of State Marco Rubio is publicly promoting a new "Trump defense deal with NATO," framing it as a "big, beautiful win for America" [1]. This action directly challenges a U.S.-Ukraine minerals agreement and secures a valuable resource for Moscow [2]. Internally, while President Trump has famously claimed he could end the Ukraine war in 24 hours, new reports suggest his "patience with Putin is wearing thin" [3].
